  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_a18109ba-868c-489a-bbd3-2c923011174e'
      });
    }

  <span id="freeText17312068820736251076" style="display:none"><b>The Vours: Evil, demonic beings that inhabit human bodies on Sorry Night, the darkest hours of the winter solstice.</b><br /><br />When Reggie reads about the Vours in a mysterious old journal, she assumes they are just the musings of an anonymous lunatic. But when her little brother, Henry, begins to act strangely, it's clear that these creatures exist beyond a madwoman's imagination, and Reggie finds out what happens when fears come to life.<br /><br />To save the people she loves, Reggie must learn to survive in a world of nightmares. Can she devour her own fears before they devour her?<br /><br /><i>The Devouring</i> is an engrossing tale of terror that will have you wondering: what if your worst fears became your living nightmare?</span>

<div id="review_58515540" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/58515540" />
    <a title=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books"><img alt=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1403239075p2/1570669.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/58515540?book_show_action=true">Jun 05, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" class="user" itemprop="url" name=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" href="/user/show/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books"> Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Older teen horror fans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=demon">demon</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=not-for-the-faint-of-heart">not-for-the-faint-of-heart</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer58515540" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8959466606959028327">I finished this book with an undecided feeling. It was a good read, and kept my interest. I'm not sure that I enjoyed it that much. A very interesting concept about creatures that take over the body of a person who is absolutely terrified on Sorry Night, which is the night of the Winter Solstice. I heard about this book, and read some positive reviews, and decided to go for it. I have no regrets that I did read it, but I have to say that there were things I could have liked better about this boo</span>
  <span id="freeText8959466606959028327" style="display:none">I finished this book with an undecided feeling. It was a good read, and kept my interest. I'm not sure that I enjoyed it that much. A very interesting concept about creatures that take over the body of a person who is absolutely terrified on Sorry Night, which is the night of the Winter Solstice. I heard about this book, and read some positive reviews, and decided to go for it. I have no regrets that I did read it, but I have to say that there were things I could have liked better about this book. The opening was excellent, really unnerving me. I started this book right before bedtime, and I had to read a little bit of a romance book before I turned off the light and went to sleep. It sets the reader up to know this wouldn't be an especially gentle horror story.<br /><br /><br />When I asked myself what didn't quite ring true to me about this story, I am encouraged to go and analyze it. I didn't dislike the main characters. Reggie was a sympathetic protagonist. She's been forced to grow up too fast, coerced/encouraged by her father to take the role of her mother, who left the family and has not returned. She's only fifteen and she wants to do the normal things that a fifteen year old does, but she is pretty much forced to raise her younger brother, Henry, who is eight, since her father works a demanding construction contracting job (and is emotionally withdrawn). Going into the story, you feel her longing to be 'normal' and to not have the weight of the world on her shoulders. Mixed in is some resentment towards her younger brother, who has gotten more clingy, instead of more independent. This sets the stage for what will happen in this sibling relationship.<br /><br />Reggie works in a small bookstore that caters towards the horror/gothic tastes. She unpacks a box of books and finds a diary-looking book in the box called The Devouring, which she decides to read, with her best friend Aaron on Sorry Night. She and Aaron expose themselves to their individual worst phobias and chant the mysterious poem at the beginning of the journal. This somehow seems to activate the vour to take her brother's soul, for he is the most frightened in the house. Reggie puts him to bed and he sits in the dark, afraid out of his mind, easy prey for this evil being.<br /><br />From there this story turns into a 'Bad Seed' kind of narrative, as Henry becomes increasingly not like himself. He becomes cruel and violent, commiting acts that are increasingly disturbing. Reggie doesn't put two and two together at first, which I found annoying. Clearly her brother is not acting normal, and his skin becomes very cold to the touch. It takes too long for her to get a clue, but I was glad that she is scolded by her boss at the bookstore, Eben, for diddling around with this journal, and she didn't know what she was doing.<br /><br />Reggie has to face her worst fears and delve into the fearscape where her brother's consciousness has been entrapped, in order to get him back and to save him from the Vours. They are after her as well. They thrive on fear, and Reggie has walked a tightrope of being brave (she's a major horror buff) and fighting her real-life fears. I thought this was a good message about not letting your fears control you, and facing the truth instead of avoiding the acceptance of things that you don't want to face and you know you cannot change.<br /><br />I liked Reggie's buddy, Aaron, who is a bit of a geek, and who shares her love of horror movies, but also has a fascination with serial killers. He is a true friend to her the whole time, and I got the impression he might have a crush on Reggie, although she's fixated on footballer player and popular kid, Quinn. Aaron is in for the long haul, facing danger and his devastating fear of drowning, to help Reggie get her brother's soul back and to vanquish the vour that is controlling his body.<br /><br />What I didn't particularly care for in this story: <br /><br /> I felt that Reggie and Henry's dad was too one-dimensional. He seemed like a plot point, only coming around to scold Reggie for not doing enough, and to treat Reggie badly when he starts to believe the Un-Henry's lies. He didn't seem all that real to me, and wasn't that loving. Okay, I can acknowledge that he was in a bad place, having lost his wife, and trying to raise his kids without her. But there wasn't enough signs of his love for his kids shining through.<br /><br /> Also I wished there was more closure about their mom disappearing. You don't really get too much information, other than she's gone, and Reggie secretly wished she was dead, rather than face that her mom ran out on her. I would like to understand what was motivating this flight. We know that Reggie was close to her mom, and they had girl talk session in the bathroom when she cut Reggie's hair. That's why I didn't understand what prompted her to leave, and there didn't seem to be any signs that she was fed up, either. The book doesn't really give enough information on this to feel like there's a whole story there, and so I am forced to see the mother as yet another poorly-fleshed out character. <br /><br />I thought the book was a tad too gruesome. There are some pretty long, detailed scenes describing acts of cruelty or the aftermath that I am not sure how appropriate they would be for a younger audience. I had some issues with them, and I'm 36 years old. I think the author is targeting the young adult audience who loves slasher movies, and these teens wouldn't have a problem with these scenes. I can't fault him on that, but it didn't seem to fit in with the somewhat gothic vours concept. It seemed to go in a 180 degree direction, in fact. <br /><br />The organic nature of the vours came out of left field, leaving me with more questions. I wasn't quite expecting that. I'm wondering how these pieces fit together, in fact. There is a sequel to this book, but I'm not sure how motivated I am to read it, at this point. I might pick it up later on to get some closure. However, I can't say I was blown away by this story, and felt motivated to commit myself to this series. However, I freely admit it was a great book to read on Halloween, and very suspenseful. <br /><br />I think Mr. Holt is a very good writer, and has a talent in horror. But unfortunately, this book doesn't get out of B grade territory for me because of the lack of depth with the parents, and also with Henry (I couldn't feel too much for them). Also, there were some parts where Henry is treated rather brutally by his sister and Aaron (because of the vour inside him) that made me squirm. It felt like child abuse (irrational of me, but there you have it). It just needed a little more depth for me to feel more strongly about it. For a basic horror book for teens that doesn't require much emotional commitment or analysis, this is a good one. I just like a little more with my reading.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8959466606959028327" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=nook">nook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=horror">horror</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer66703090" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18421358187200842365">YA Horror isn't in the same league with Adult Horror, so I'm not going to try and compare apples to carpet cleaner. There's no point.<br/><br/>This was a <i>really</i> good teen horror story. I wish I had been able to read it when I was younger, because I'm sure it would have been one of my favorites.<br/><br/>The breakdown of the story is that a girl and her best friend (who happen to love all things scary), get their hands on an old journal that they believe to be someone's idea of a joke. Maybe the first draft of a nov</span>
  <span id="freeText18421358187200842365" style="display:none">YA Horror isn't in the same league with Adult Horror, so I'm not going to try and compare apples to carpet cleaner. There's no point.<br /><br />This was a <i>really</i> good teen horror story. I wish I had been able to read it when I was younger, because I'm sure it would have been one of my favorites.<br /><br />The breakdown of the story is that a girl and her best friend (who happen to love all things scary), get their hands on an old journal that they believe to be someone's idea of a joke. Maybe the first draft of a novel they were writing. According to this book there are evil spirits who can enter and take over your body one night a year, if you are frightened enough. So in the tradition of Bloody Mary, they call the spirits up as a joke. Except they aren't scared. Unfortunately, the girl's little brother is in the house...and he is terrified.<br /><br />To adults who have been weaned on Stephen King, there is nothing here that they probably haven't seen a million times before. But to those new to the genre? <i>Brrrrrr.</i> Nothing says creepy like a possessed kid. Especially one that you love.<br /><br />This is a trilogy, so the ending has a conclusion, but you know nothing is really over for those poor kids.<br /> <br />Good stuff. It's well written, and I was chewing my nails even though I guessed the probable outcome. <br />I'd recommend it for teens looking for a spooky read, or adults looking for Horror-Lite.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="18421358187200842365" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8402261164288335025">I wouldn’t classify myself as a fan of scary things. I’ve been afraid of the dark for as long as I can remember, yes, I am still afraid of the dark. I do not like scary movies, I happened to watch It, the movie based on the novel of the same title by Steven King, when I was in elementary school, I don’t think I slept for weeks, and I still haven’t been able to watch the movie again. So, when I grabbed a copy of the Devouring by Simon Holt and read the synopsis, I have to admit I was a little sca</span>
  <span id="freeText8402261164288335025" style="display:none">I wouldn’t classify myself as a fan of scary things. I’ve been afraid of the dark for as long as I can remember, yes, I am still afraid of the dark. I do not like scary movies, I happened to watch It, the movie based on the novel of the same title by Steven King, when I was in elementary school, I don’t think I slept for weeks, and I still haven’t been able to watch the movie again. So, when I grabbed a copy of the Devouring by Simon Holt and read the synopsis, I have to admit I was a little scared to read it!<br /><br />And it was scary/freaky/suspenseful! But besides that it was a great novel! Yes, me scardy girl, enjoyed reading a “horror” novel. I can’t really compare it to any other novels of that nature, but I can say that I thought the plot was wonderfully crafted. The whole concept of the Vours was masterful! I hope I don’t run in to any of those things on Sorry Night.<br /><br />I also appreciated the fact that the novel kept the gruesome elements to a minimum. Instead of being overkill the few mentions where actually an enhancement to the tale. I’m eagerly waiting to begin the next novel in this series!<br /></span>

<div id="review_44451858" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/44451858" />
    <a title="Rachael" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1028829-rachael"><img alt="Rachael" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1245975041p2/1028829.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/44451858?book_show_action=true">Jan 26, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachael" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachael" href="/user/show/1028829-rachael">Rachael</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer44451858" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12602376680531648245">Reggie is a horror fan; she figures reading all those scary books and watching all those scary movies is a sort of preparation for the real thing, real fear. But for Reggie, real fear is just arachnophobia for example, something real she can name. So when she stumbles upon a mysterious journal detailing the horrors of certain demonic beings called Vours that take over human bodies, she dismisses it as a work of fiction. But she can’t deny the strange coincidence of her little brother Henry actin</span>
  <span id="freeText12602376680531648245" style="display:none">Reggie is a horror fan; she figures reading all those scary books and watching all those scary movies is a sort of preparation for the real thing, real fear. But for Reggie, real fear is just arachnophobia for example, something real she can name. So when she stumbles upon a mysterious journal detailing the horrors of certain demonic beings called Vours that take over human bodies, she dismisses it as a work of fiction. But she can’t deny the strange coincidence of her little brother Henry acting very strangely—and after Sorry Night, the only time that Vours can invade bodies. And when Henry’s behavior becomes more erratic and destructive, Reggie realizes that she had no idea what real fear was before—because now, she’s living it.<br /><br />The Devouring is a suspenseful paranormal novel with elements of horror. Its strongest point is by far its unique plot, which I found exciting, original, and unpredictable with its combination of mystery, familiar problems, and all-encompassing fear. The characters, on the other hand, are a bit hard to connect with, even Reggie with her fierce determination. She was a little too easily blinded by cute popular boys and seemed to be spooked easily despite her claims to have conquered her fears. Another problem I have was that I often felt removed from the story despite vivid and horrifying details because it felt so unreal. Part of this is due to how fast paced The Devouring is; Reggie had to adapt, almost too quickly sometimes it seemed, to each new situation. I am a little disappointed, because thought The Devouring would’ve been better, but it is still an interesting read with a scientific twist to fear.<br /><br />Fans of Peeps and The Midnighters trilogy, both by Scott Westerfeld, and The Summoning by Kelley Armstrong will likely enjoy this intriguing read.<br /><br />reposted from <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://thebookmuncher.blogspot.com">http://thebookmuncher.blogspot.com</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="12602376680531648245" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

And, I am really glad that this book lived up to the hype I put in my brain. This isn’t a popular series. In fact, only three of my friends have read and rated this book. Crazy, right?<br /><br /><i>The Devouring</i> follows a broken family. Reggie is in high school and has to fill the role her mother had before she left the family. Her father is a workaholic and she had a little brother, Henry. She goes to school, cooks, cleans, takes care of her brother, and also works at a bookstore. At her job, she finds a weird journal with an insane story about Sorry Night.<br /><br />Sorry Night is when the Vours can come into human bodies. Vours are demonic beings that make people live their worst fears.<br /><br />Reggie doesn’t take the story seriously until she has to.<br /><br />I read this book wayyy back in high school and I remember really enjoying it. Enough that I found and bought all three books. I don’t remember reading the whole series, but I must have since they’re all rated by me on Goodreads.<br /><br />It was a funny and creepy book. I loved reading it in the mornings while I drink my coffee. When I had to leave for practicum or work, I couldn’t wait until the next morning so I could pick it right back up. The story was fun. The characters were great. And I can’t wait to rediscover where the rest of the books take me.</span>

<div id="review_31926264" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/31926264" />
    <a title="Lucy " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45923-lucy"><img alt="Lucy " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1300985055p2/45923.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/31926264?book_show_action=true">Sep 03, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lucy " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lucy " href="/user/show/45923-lucy">Lucy </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Darren Shan fans, teen horror fans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45923-lucy?shelf=teen">teen</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45923-lucy?shelf=supernatural">supernatural</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45923-lucy?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer31926264" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16609531119749379578">Regina Halloway loves scary stories. She reads them compulsively--she even works in a horror book store. Sometimes, she thinks she might be reading them to distract her from the truly scary things in her life--like the fact that her mom ran out on them, and they haven't heard from her in over a year, or the fact that her father is more and more distant every day. Or the fact that she is singlehandedly raising her little brother, Henry.<br/><br/>But mostly, Reggie just reads horror because she loves it. An</span>
  <span id="freeText16609531119749379578" style="display:none">Regina Halloway loves scary stories. She reads them compulsively--she even works in a horror book store. Sometimes, she thinks she might be reading them to distract her from the truly scary things in her life--like the fact that her mom ran out on them, and they haven't heard from her in over a year, or the fact that her father is more and more distant every day. Or the fact that she is singlehandedly raising her little brother, Henry.<br /><br />But mostly, Reggie just reads horror because she loves it. And when she finds an old journal called The Devouring, she brings it home and reads it. It tells of creatures called Vours that can attack people through their fears, and then inhabit their bodies. They come into our world on Sorry Night, the eve of the winter solstice.<br /><br />Naturally, Reggie and her best friend Aaron can't resist summoning the Vours on Sorry Night. But they aren't the ones who are possessed--instead, Reggie's little brother Henry starts acting stranger and stranger, until Reggie realizes that he's not Henry anymore--he's something older and darker. Something terrifying.<br /><br />To save her brother, Reggie will have to face her deepest fears.<br /><br />The writing in this book is not strong, and it nearly lost me with its clunkiness in the first couple of chapters. It felt a little cliche and tired, and I could predict exactly what would happen.<br /><br />But then the horror starts, and damned if this book isn't scary. It's truly, terrifyingly scary. At one point, I almost had to stop reading and take a breath.<br /><br />So it's not a work of great literature. What it is is a top notch teen horror novel. Fans of Darren Shan will eat this up.<br /><br />A warning--though this book does have a satisfying ending, it's the jumping-off point of a series, and is open-ended. I definitly want to read more.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16609531119749379578" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5867479146244155443">This is an extremely well written horror story that kept me cringing and reading late into the night. It concerns Regina and her younger brother Henry, who has become possessed by a demon-like entity called a Vour. Adults are pretty much absent in the picture (with one mysterious exception), so it's up to Reggie to figure out how to save her brother. This is one creepy book, and it leaves plenty of leeway for this to turn into a series. Yes, there's even a clown involved (ugh!). I'd liken it to </span>
  <span id="freeText5867479146244155443" style="display:none">This is an extremely well written horror story that kept me cringing and reading late into the night. It concerns Regina and her younger brother Henry, who has become possessed by a demon-like entity called a Vour. Adults are pretty much absent in the picture (with one mysterious exception), so it's up to Reggie to figure out how to save her brother. This is one creepy book, and it leaves plenty of leeway for this to turn into a series. Yes, there's even a clown involved (ugh!). I'd liken it to John Saul's work. Because of some very graphic horror content I wouldn't recommend anyone under 16, or anyone alone in a house short on lighting and door locks, reading it. </span>

<div id="review_121123877" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/121123877" />
    <a title="YA Reads Book Reviews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1764232-ya-reads-book-reviews"><img alt="YA Reads Book Reviews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1285429046p2/1764232.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/121123877?book_show_action=true">Sep 11, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="YA Reads Book Reviews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="YA Reads Book Reviews" href="/user/show/1764232-ya-reads-book-reviews">YA Reads Book Reviews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer121123877" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer553809226765165745">As far as covers go, The Devouring is pretty spectacular. In fact, it’s so good that I picked it up off the shelf in the store and decided I was going to buy it even before I looked at the blurb. Apart from being visually stimulating, it manages to capture the real essence of the story without giving too much away.<br/><br/>The blurb is pretty enticing as well. Check this out:<br/><br/>Vours:<br/>Evil, demonic beings that inhabit human bodies on Sorry Night, the darkest hours of the winter solstice.<br/><br/>This isn’t how the ho</span>
  <span id="freeText553809226765165745" style="display:none">As far as covers go, The Devouring is pretty spectacular. In fact, it’s so good that I picked it up off the shelf in the store and decided I was going to buy it even before I looked at the blurb. Apart from being visually stimulating, it manages to capture the real essence of the story without giving too much away.<br /><br />The blurb is pretty enticing as well. Check this out:<br /><br />Vours:<br />Evil, demonic beings that inhabit human bodies on Sorry Night, the darkest hours of the winter solstice.<br /><br />This isn’t how the horror ended for us –<br />This is how it began.<br /><br />When Reggie reads about the Vours in a mysterious old journal, she assumes they are just the musings of an anonymous lunatic. But when her little brother, Henry, begins to act strangely, it’s clear that these creatures exist beyond a madwoman’s imagination, and Reggie finds out what happens when fears come to life. To save the people she loves, Reggie must learn to survive in a world of nightmares. Can she devour her own fears before they devour her?<br /><br />The Devouring is an engrossing tale of terror that will have you wondering: what if your worst fears became your living nightmare?<br /><br />Sounds awesome, right? Well, I thought so anyway. Unfortunately, now that I’ve finished reading it, I’m not quite sure what to think. Firstly, let me just say that I didn’t think it was bad. Not at all. But there is just something about it that isn’t sitting right with me.<br /><br />The characters are all likable enough, yet they don’t seem individual enough, there is not a whole lot that separate them from each other in my mind. For me to consider a book astonishing, the characters really need to jump off the page and present themselves as independent, unique individuals. That doesn’t really happen for me with The Devouring. However, I’m not prepared to say that I don’t like the characters, because I do. Or maybe it’s just that there isn’t anything exceptionally unlikable about them, I can’t quite tell. Either way, they didn’t leave a huge impression.<br /><br />Everything happens pretty fast, too. There isn’t a whole lot of build up, which for some, might be a good thing. I, however, am a big fan of the build up. I love anticipation and surprise. Although it’s not predictable, per se, The Devouring didn’t have me sitting on the edge of my seat. Yet, at the same time, I didn’t want to put it down.<br /><br />Can you see what I’m saying here? It wasn’t bad, not by a long shot, but it wasn’t outstanding either, you know? I do think that it would make a really awesome film, however. Visually, I think it would be a real creeper. But as words, well, it falls a little short of creepy.<br /><br />Give it a go. I’m interested in your thoughts!</span>
  <a data-text-id="553809226765165745" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Becky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50448-becky"><img alt="Becky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1175789489p2/50448.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/32189703?book_show_action=true">Sep 06, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Becky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Becky" href="/user/show/50448-becky">Becky</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer32189703" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer9386660191494767117">Holt, Simon. 2008. The Devouring: Sorry Night.<br/><br/>"Stop, Reggie!" Henry barked from beneath his quilt. "Don't read anymore!" Regina Halloway shut the book. (5)<br/><br/>Regina--called Reggie by most of her friends and family--loves to read horror. Loves it. So much so that she works at a used bookstore devoted to the genre. But perhaps Reggie should have been a bit more thoughtful as to what she was reading her younger--and much more gullible--brother, Henry. Then again, Regina hadn't any idea that her latest</span>
  <span id="freeText9386660191494767117" style="display:none">Holt, Simon. 2008. The Devouring: Sorry Night.<br /><br />"Stop, Reggie!" Henry barked from beneath his quilt. "Don't read anymore!" Regina Halloway shut the book. (5)<br /><br />Regina--called Reggie by most of her friends and family--loves to read horror. Loves it. So much so that she works at a used bookstore devoted to the genre. But perhaps Reggie should have been a bit more thoughtful as to what she was reading her younger--and much more gullible--brother, Henry. Then again, Regina hadn't any idea that her latest book, an old journal she found while unpacking boxes for the store, was nonfiction. That the Vours were real.<br /><br />When Dark creeps in and eats the light, Bury your fears on Sorry Night. For in the winter's blackest hours Comes the feasting of the Vours. No one can see it, the life they stole, Your body's here but not your soul...(4)<br /><br />See. Not the stuff for bedtime stories for your younger brother, right? Maybe this would have turned out just fine...if only...if only she wasn't reading it the night before "Sorry Night" the Winter Solstice, December 22nd. If only her brother hadn't been so very frightened at the thought that the Vours were real and coming for him...if only Reggie hadn't left him alone the next night to go off in pursuit of her own chills and thrills...<br /><br />Then again, if she had, The Devouring wouldn't be such a chilling book.<br /><br />For more about The Devouring, read my weekly geeks post where Nymeth interviewed me about the book.<br /><br />© Becky Laney of Becky's Book Reviews</span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2176078-vania?shelf=my-shelf">my-shelf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer50946951" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2255484808462947580">This book is instantly chilling. I was sucked in int he deep abyss of Reggie's fears. This tale is dark and deep, chilling me to the bone. A gripping tale of overcoming your deepest darkest fears turning them in on themselves.<br/><br/>Reggie starts off as a weaker character growing stronger and more assertive through her love and devotion for her little brother. She begins the novel with a theory that proves useful later: she immerses herself in horror and fright through movies and literature, knowing th</span>
  <span id="freeText2255484808462947580" style="display:none">This book is instantly chilling. I was sucked in int he deep abyss of Reggie's fears. This tale is dark and deep, chilling me to the bone. A gripping tale of overcoming your deepest darkest fears turning them in on themselves.<br /><br />Reggie starts off as a weaker character growing stronger and more assertive through her love and devotion for her little brother. She begins the novel with a theory that proves useful later: she immerses herself in horror and fright through movies and literature, knowing that facing your fears, makes you stronger. Her skittish best friend Aaron on the other hand has a hard time overcoming that which scares him the most. His loyalty proves to be his best defense against the frightful beings that overtake and consume their fears. Those monstrous things that can take full control of their bodies, gaining power and strength through their fright and terror.<br /><br />The story is race for control. Control of the body and mind that the Vours (those monstrous beings that feed on nightmares) are so eager to keep and protect, no matter the cost. Life or death. It is a high speed nightmare of a story with the most hidden, darkest and most frightful nightmares one can imagine. Skin crawling imagery full of ghoulish tableau of nightmarish after nightmarish scenarios. So tormenting that I had to read it during the day.The novel grips you and I was so engrossed in this ghoulish and utterly frightful tale.<br /><br />Some characters liek Reggie are well fleshed out, full of life. Others like Eben and Aaron left me wanting more. I was left in the dark not knowing much about the characters themselves, leaving them mere props in Reggie's quest to save her brother. Henry, Reggie's brother, was by far the creepiest little kid I have ever read about. He was so eerily bewitching and haunting at the same time. I wanted to read more of his torment and more of the deep, dark, secret Vour.<br /><br />The story was an intrigue and a nightmare. A fast paced race into nightmares and fears, with life and death walking a thin line.<br /><br />Now some creepy quotes:<br />"The scraping noise of a hatchet blade across glass sent her racing deeper into the maze. This time no sawdust signaled the way out. She reached one dead end after another, surrounded by even more freakish reflections: her father's head severed on a platter with apple in his mouth, her mother rocking a demon infant..." (p186)<br />AND<br />"Mom raised the scissors high. They flashed in the light like a silver-winged bird, and then plunged them into her own wrist. She offered her arm to Reggie like a bloody sacrifice."<br /><br /><br />I give this book a 88/100 B+<br />Characters-16<br />Plot- 19<br />Writing-17<br />Originality-18<br />Re-Readability- 18</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3589919-jessica-saylor?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer135949751" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16108260791844598357"><b>Quick Overview:</b> With an entrancing plot but slightly underdeveloped characters, The Devouring was a fun read that left a lot of room for a great series. <br/><br/>This book was nothing like I expected it to be. Looking back, I have no idea why I didn't pick this book up sooner. It has been sitting on my shelves for probably about a year, and I just ran my hand across it without taking a second look every time. If you are having the same problem, don't hesitate. This book is worth the read. <br/><br/>The Devouring h</span>
  <span id="freeText16108260791844598357" style="display:none"><b>Quick Overview:</b> With an entrancing plot but slightly underdeveloped characters, The Devouring was a fun read that left a lot of room for a great series. <br /><br />This book was nothing like I expected it to be. Looking back, I have no idea why I didn't pick this book up sooner. It has been sitting on my shelves for probably about a year, and I just ran my hand across it without taking a second look every time. If you are having the same problem, don't hesitate. This book is worth the read. <br /><br />The Devouring has such an exciting plot. One of my favorite things about it, was the creepy factor. It takes a lot for a book to creep me out, but the voices and thoughts that Holt put into my head had me shivering and leaving on a night light (well, I have one anyways, but I was particularly grateful for it these last few nights). <br /><br />I felt that the characters were a little underdeveloped. I couldn't tell you much about the main character except that she is into cute boys and likes anything to do with horror. I could tell you even less about other main characters Eden and Aaron. The only character that really did it for me was Henry, and that could just be because I have a soft spot for cute little boys. They remind me of my nephew so I am constantly on their side in books.<br /><br />The Devouring was a great series beginning. There wasn't much particularly special about the novel itself, it wasn't absolutely amazing and it wasn't bad at all either. It was just a fun read that left a lot of room for a great series. <br /><br /><b>Parental Suggestion:</b> Though the eerie setting and nightmarish themes in The Devouring are pretty stinking creepy, there is nothing in this book that is inappropriate for teenagers 13 and older. <br /><br /><i>First Line: "On sorry night, just a few nights before Christmas, you have to snuff the lamps, douse the flames in the fireplace, and spend the night in the cold and dark."<br />-Page One</i><br /><br />Plot: 19/20<br />Characters: 18/20<br />Creativity: 18/20<br />Writing: 16/20<br />Ending: 7/10<br />Cover: 8/10<br />=86/100, B</span>

<div id="review_98414562" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/98414562" />
    <a title="Sensitivemuse" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2434215-sensitivemuse"><img alt="Sensitivemuse" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1245554798p2/2434215.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/98414562?book_show_action=true">Apr 13, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sensitivemuse" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sensitivemuse" href="/user/show/2434215-sensitivemuse">Sensitivemuse</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer98414562" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14368586262816924778">This book was so good I wanted to stay up at night to finish it. The prologue was so good and gripping that I had to continue reading it to see what would happen. The book had all the makings to become a horror movie itself. The writing was great and an easy read. It had very well written descriptions of horror scenes which is enough to put the reader on edge. Some parts were so well written I found myself reacting to it out loud while reading. <br/><br/>Fear is the main theme here, and Reggie has a giant</span>
  <span id="freeText14368586262816924778" style="display:none">This book was so good I wanted to stay up at night to finish it. The prologue was so good and gripping that I had to continue reading it to see what would happen. The book had all the makings to become a horror movie itself. The writing was great and an easy read. It had very well written descriptions of horror scenes which is enough to put the reader on edge. Some parts were so well written I found myself reacting to it out loud while reading. <br /><br />Fear is the main theme here, and Reggie has a giant phobia of spiders. Naturally, there are many scenes which include spiders. I'm rather scared of spiders myself and I could just feel my skin crawl as I read the parts where Reggie is constantly terrorized by them. As said before, the horror scenes are excellent and picturing them isn't so hard. It brings the reader right into the book as if one was beside Reggie herself. <br /><br />I like Reggie. She's the typical horror heroine you find in horror movies. Strong, attempting to live life as normal as possible, until the Vours come in and turn her life upside down. Her friend Aaron is also, your typical side kick in a horror movie who is the brains and helps Reggie get to the bottom of understand and figuring out the Vours. Then there's Eben, who's the mysterious good guy but with a horrible secret. <br /><br />However, like any horror movie, it doesn't stop there. There is a second book out (called Soulstice) which I am definitely getting once I have the chance to. The Devouring is definitely worth reading if you feel like reading something creepy and terrifying. Yet, there are still questions to be answered. There is blood and gore in the book. So those that aren't partial to it should avoid this book. However those that want a scare should definitely pick this up. <br /><br />Overall, one of my favorite reads of this year. I am glad I picked this book up. I was pleasantly scared.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14368586262816924778" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_65943505" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/65943505" />
    <a title="Natalie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1969199-natalie"><img alt="Natalie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1427062916p2/1969199.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/65943505?book_show_action=true">Aug 02, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natalie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natalie" href="/user/show/1969199-natalie">Natalie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer65943505" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1698492079534220606"><i>“When dark creeps in and eats the light, bury your fears on Sorry Night. For in the winter’s blackest hours, comes the feassting of the Vours. No one can see it, the life they stole. Your body’s here, but not your soul…”</i><br/><br/>Reggie has always been a fan of the gothic, the supernatural, the horrific. One day, while working at the local bookstore, she comes across a book called The Devouring and, thinking it’s just another horror novel, takes it home. As Reggie and her best friend, Aaron, peruse the bo</span>
  <span id="freeText1698492079534220606" style="display:none"><i>“When dark creeps in and eats the light, bury your fears on Sorry Night. For in the winter’s blackest hours, comes the feassting of the Vours. No one can see it, the life they stole. Your body’s here, but not your soul…”</i><br /><br />Reggie has always been a fan of the gothic, the supernatural, the horrific. One day, while working at the local bookstore, she comes across a book called The Devouring and, thinking it’s just another horror novel, takes it home. As Reggie and her best friend, Aaron, peruse the book, they discover the world of the Vours, demonic creatures who possess humans by preying off of fear.<br /><br />For Reggie and Aaron, it’s all just fun and games, until Reggie’s little brother, Henry, starts exhibiting strange behavior. Then, bad things start happening. Henry’s babysitter turns up dead, and Reggie finds Henry’s pet hamster in the toilet with a broken neck. Henry begins lying to their father, getting Reggie in trouble for things she didn’t do. When Reggie starts experiencing fear-induced hallucinations, she begins to wonder if the Vours really are just storybook monsters after all.<br /><br />The Devouring is a compelling young adult thriller that focuses on the element of fear. Even though the Vours are fictional beings, I found it easy to relate to the fear described in the book, mainly because fear is a natural reaction that all of us, as humans, experience at one time or another. In addition, The Devouring doesn’t just focus on supernatural issues, but normal, teenage problems that the characters face as well. The book was very well-written and suspenseful, and kept me turning pages the entire time. Be warned though, it does end with a cliffhanger, leading into Holt’s second book in the series, The Soulstice.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_220023977" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/220023977" />
    <a title="Alexandra" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4538194-alexandra"><img alt="Alexandra" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599115695p2/4538194.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/220023977?book_show_action=true">Oct 06, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alexandra" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alexandra" href="/user/show/4538194-alexandra">Alexandra</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer220023977" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16736577523257663235">This is one of those books that I had heard so many awesome things about, bought at a Borders closing sale, and then left to sit on my bookshelf for months and months. Why did I do that?! <br/>It was SO good! <br/><br/>The Devouring is a YA horror novel, but it's actually really creepy and well written. I like the way Simon Holt's mind works. From the very first page, I was sucked right into this story. <br/><br/>The <i>School Library Journal</i> compares Simon Holt to R.L. Stine which I guess I can see, but The Devouring is m</span>
  <span id="freeText16736577523257663235" style="display:none">This is one of those books that I had heard so many awesome things about, bought at a Borders closing sale, and then left to sit on my bookshelf for months and months. Why did I do that?! <br />It was SO good! <br /><br />The Devouring is a YA horror novel, but it's actually really creepy and well written. I like the way Simon Holt's mind works. From the very first page, I was sucked right into this story. <br /><br />The <i>School Library Journal</i> compares Simon Holt to R.L. Stine which I guess I can see, but The Devouring is much more advanced than a Goosebumps book, I'll tell you that right now. And much more detailed. Don't get me wrong, I used to love Goosebumps books. But when I was in 2nd and 3rd grade. I wouldn't want to read them now. So I wouldn't want the comparison to R.L. Stine to deter older readers from this book, because The Devouring is definitely more substantial. <br /><br />It takes place in a tiny town called Cutter's Wedge, during the wintertime. That's something that I found really cool about this book because it is very Halloween-y (a.k.a appropriate to read during the Halloween season) but it also takes place during the Winter Solstice and Christmas so it would also be a fun read to pick up in December. Very versatile ;)<br /><br />The Devouring also has a really good message to it, which is essentially to face your fear and not let it get the best of you &amp; if you can look what scares you in the eye and not back down or let it overcome you, then you will come out on top, which I really liked. Great read :D</span>
  <a data-text-id="16736577523257663235" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_76813380" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/76813380" />
    <a title="Nely" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1440151-nely"><img alt="Nely" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1271166357p2/1440151.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/76813380?book_show_action=true">Nov 05, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nely" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nely" href="/user/show/1440151-nely">Nely</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1440151-nely?shelf=library">library</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer76813380" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14710947844764936419">I really can't say I am a fan of things scary. I avoid scary movies like the plague. To be quite honest, I always tell the hubs "if we are ever caught in a scary movie-type scenario, run with the kids, I'm going to be the one who trips and falls and gets keeeled by the monster".<br/><br/>With that said, The Devouring, was all that and a bag of chips for me. I was scared, I was excited, I was at the edge-of-my-seat, I was taken in from the start and spit out at the end... and then I couldn't stop thinking </span>
  <span id="freeText14710947844764936419" style="display:none">I really can't say I am a fan of things scary. I avoid scary movies like the plague. To be quite honest, I always tell the hubs "if we are ever caught in a scary movie-type scenario, run with the kids, I'm going to be the one who trips and falls and gets keeeled by the monster".<br /><br />With that said, The Devouring, was all that and a bag of chips for me. I was scared, I was excited, I was at the edge-of-my-seat, I was taken in from the start and spit out at the end... and then I couldn't stop thinking about it. There were plenty of parts that gave me goosebumps and had me looking for a bright, sunny spot to read it in.<br /><br />I really liked Reggie. I love her go get 'em attitude. She had no fears when it came to standing up for those she loves. I also loved her relationship with her BFF and sidekick, Aaron. Hopefully a love interest will spark between the two in the next book (keeping fingers crossed).<br /><br />I will forewarn though, this is not for the faint of heart. There were some instances that were pretty gruesome - I didn't think it was overkill, but I can see where some might. This is definitely geared for the older teen - Mr. Holt's writing is simple, to the point, and there is some mild violence with hardly any bad language. I personally think it's a great read for lovers of horror / slasher movies no matter the age. It really was deliciously creepy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14710947844764936419" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Holt does an excellent job really creating images from words. I can't say I'm a huge horror fan. But, this is the first book I've read on the subject so maybe my opinion is based on lack of exposure. Great book, amazing yet terrifying story.<br /><br />Regina and her best friend Aaron are all about anything scary. Regina is a high school freshman who works part time at a book store and comes across a journal titled "The Devouring." Together they discover that there maybe nothing more frightening than your worst fears as nightmares start becoming reality. </span>

<div id="review_2658732700" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2658732700" />
    <a title="Tiffany" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12655196-tiffany"><img alt="Tiffany" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1347141750p2/12655196.jpg" /></a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2658732700" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14672253643537454598">3.5, rounded up to 4.<br/>I guess I should start out by saying that horror isn't really my thing, since I'm a scaredy cat. I don't read much horror, but I was curious after reading some of the reviews. This book didn't spook me, but it was creepy, and I enjoyed the visuals. The Devouring was really good for scary and grotesque visuals. I found this book enjoyable, and I'll likely put its sequel in my to-read list, but it's not high-priority read for me. Horror isn't my thing, and this book didn't cha</span>
  <span id="freeText14672253643537454598" style="display:none">3.5, rounded up to 4.<br />I guess I should start out by saying that horror isn't really my thing, since I'm a scaredy cat. I don't read much horror, but I was curious after reading some of the reviews. This book didn't spook me, but it was creepy, and I enjoyed the visuals. The Devouring was really good for scary and grotesque visuals. I found this book enjoyable, and I'll likely put its sequel in my to-read list, but it's not high-priority read for me. Horror isn't my thing, and this book didn't change that for me. Still a pretty good book, though.</span>

  <span id="freeText1115339289701448983" style="display:none">I read this as a "Read a scary book" challenge. And Im glad I didnt read it at night home alone although Ive heard multiple young-adults say that it isnt scary at all. Yes it is. Im gonna have nightmares.<br /><br />I didnt expect much of it and thanks to that Im pleasantly surprised. There were many cliches and some events were predictable but it had its twists and turns where I was really holymoly surprised. <br /><br />I will keep recommending this book to anyone interested in horror in my library and Ill keep waiting for more YA books like this to be translated to Estonian. </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('3PT5zAfy27ZgYHz/SiqxQpOlo9iXN7+SUMCYFjyRjYz55y27HJwyMyHgEwFHerwyjyIy7DnCre5l+0Q34iRkqQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('mC0F65Mq8CTi8aCO8u1y1gtLtpcAp3ZZbA3TX3XYrXe9PtGciEQZoaNxz3D/vX+mF8wno65SZCVZNg9+q21EUg==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer9521443711678916761">Simon Holt's writing career began with a horror fanzine in high school the publishing of which overheated the school's photocopier. Undaunted by detention, he's continues to pursue writing ever since. Holt supported himself as a hostel night clerk and a handbag salesman before becoming a full-time novelist. A comic book collector and amateur musician, he makes his home in Chicago.</span>
